(plaintiffs, name, it) [Under the Quiet Title Act of 1972 (QTA), 1 the United States, subject to certain exceptions, has waived its sovereign [461 U.S. 273, 276] � immunity and has permitted plaintiffs to name it as a party defendant in civil actions to adjudicate title disputes involving real property in which the United States claims an interest.]
(1 United States, subject to, certain exceptions) [Under the Quiet Title Act of 1972 (QTA), 1 the United States, subject to certain exceptions, has waived its sovereign [461 U.S. 273, 276] � immunity and has permitted plaintiffs to name it as a party defendant in civil actions to adjudicate title disputes involving real property in which the United States claims an interest.]
(party defendant, is in, civil actions adjudicate) [Under the Quiet Title Act of 1972 (QTA), 1 the United States, subject to certain exceptions, has waived its sovereign [461 U.S. 273, 276] � immunity and has permitted plaintiffs to name it as a party defendant in civil actions to adjudicate title disputes involving real property in which the United States claims an interest.]
(two separate issues, concerning, QTA) [These cases present two separate issues concerning the QTA.]
(cases, present, two issues) [These cases present two separate issues concerning the QTA.]
(two issues, concerning, QTA) [These cases present two separate issues concerning the QTA.]

(Dominion, construing grants, held) [[ Footnote 5 ] Cf. United States v. Oregon, 295 U.S. 1, 14 (1935) ("Dominion over navigable waters and property in the soil under them are so identified with the sovereign power of government that a presumption against their separation from sovereignty must be indulged, in construing either grants by the sovereign of the lands to be held in private ownership or transfer of sovereignty itself. . . .]

(title, passes upon, admission to Union) [For that reason, upon the admission of a State to the Union, the title of the United States to lands underlying navigable waters within the States passes to it, as incident to the transfer to the State of local sovereignty, and is subject only to the paramount power of the United States to control such waters for purposes of navigation in interstate and foreign commerce").]
(title, passes upon, admission of State to Union) [For that reason, upon the admission of a State to the Union, the title of the United States to lands underlying navigable waters within the States passes to it, as incident to the transfer to the State of local sovereignty, and is subject only to the paramount power of the United States to control such waters for purposes of navigation in interstate and foreign commerce").]
(title, passes upon, admission) [For that reason, upon the admission of a State to the Union, the title of the United States to lands underlying navigable waters within the States passes to it, as incident to the transfer to the State of local sovereignty, and is subject only to the paramount power of the United States to control such waters for purposes of navigation in interstate and foreign commerce").]
(title, passes upon, admission of State) [For that reason, upon the admission of a State to the Union, the title of the United States to lands underlying navigable waters within the States passes to it, as incident to the transfer to the State of local sovereignty, and is subject only to the paramount power of the United States to control such waters for purposes of navigation in interstate and foreign commerce").]
(title, passes For, reason) [For that reason, upon the admission of a State to the Union, the title of the United States to lands underlying navigable waters within the States passes to it, as incident to the transfer to the State of local sovereignty, and is subject only to the paramount power of the United States to control such waters for purposes of navigation in interstate and foreign commerce").]

(It, is, determined) [30, 43 U.S.C. 1311(a), Congress provided: "It is determined and declared to be in the public interest that (1) title to and ownership of the lands beneath navigable waters within the boundaries of the respective States, and the natural resources within such lands and waters, and (2) the right and power to manage, administer, lease, develop, and use the said lands and natural resources all in accordance with applicable State law be, and they are, subject to the provisions hereof, recognized, confirmed, established, and vested in and assigned to the respective States . . . ." [461 U.S. 273, 300]]

[461 U.S. 273, 300]]
